  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6f98b1ec-af76-4d24-8753-b4c4393adba1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17826132874084971918"><i>Alternate cover for this ISBN can be found <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22456224-the-lightning-thief' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a></i><br/><br/>Percy Jackson is a good kid, but he can't seem to focus on his schoolwork or control his temper. And lately, being away at boarding school is only getting worse - Percy could have sworn his pre-algebra teacher turned into a monster and tried to kill him. When Percy's mom finds out, she knows it's time that he knew the truth ab</span>
  <span id="freeText17826132874084971918" style="display:none"><i>Alternate cover for this ISBN can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22456224-the-lightning-thief" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></i><br /><br />Percy Jackson is a good kid, but he can't seem to focus on his schoolwork or control his temper. And lately, being away at boarding school is only getting worse - Percy could have sworn his pre-algebra teacher turned into a monster and tried to kill him. When Percy's mom finds out, she knows it's time that he knew the truth about where he came from, and that he go to the one place he'll be safe. She sends Percy to Camp Half Blood, a summer camp for demigods (on Long Island), where he learns that the father he never knew is Poseidon, God of the Sea. Soon a mystery unfolds and together with his friends—one a satyr and the other the demigod daughter of Athena - Percy sets out on a quest across the United States to reach the gates of the Underworld (located in a recording studio in Hollywood) and prevent a catastrophic war between the gods.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17826132874084971918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/34487388-makenzie"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/34487388-makenzie">Makenzie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">First off, the movies do not do the books justice :)<br/><br/>But yes, definitely read the books! I'm a teenager and I read the books a few years ago, but to th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">First off, the movies do not do the books justice :)<br /><br />But yes, definitely read the books! I'm a teenager and I read the books a few years ago, but to this day it's one of my all-time favorite series. Riordan is an amazing writer, and once you start his books, you can't put them down! He does a great job with combining mythology with the modern day, so the stories seem all the more realistic.<br /><br />While the first book is projected towards a younger audience, it's still action-packed and captivating. As the series progresses, Percy, the main character, grows and gets older so by the final book in the series he's 16, so as he matures, the books get older as well. <br /><br />I also recommend these books because Rick has a follow-up series, called the Heroes of Olympus Series, which is for an older audience. Some of the characters from the Percy Jackson series carry over, so I recommend reading the first series to better understand the second (and I definitely recommend reading the follow-up series because it's just as good, if not better than the first). <br /><br />Hope this helped!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5661715-ela?shelf=movie-tie-in">movie-tie-in</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178143309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3595789888454258490">I'm slightly ashamed to say that I watched the movie before I read the book. But I'm even more ashamed that I watched the movie only to experience the hotness that is Logan Lerman.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351823i/705376.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But, come on! Someone tell me that <i> this </i>, is not hot:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/499665.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Really. What did I tell you? (I do imagine that you probably won't read the rest of the review anf just stare at this gif instead, but that's no reason not to like my review! :D)<br/><br/>But, I really have to thank Logan. I really do. Because without his unfreakingbelieveabl</span>
  <span id="freeText3595789888454258490" style="display:none">I'm slightly ashamed to say that I watched the movie before I read the book. But I'm even more ashamed that I watched the movie only to experience the hotness that is Logan Lerman.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351823i/705376.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But, come on! Someone tell me that <i> this </i>, is not hot:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/499665.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Really. What did I tell you? (I do imagine that you probably won't read the rest of the review anf just stare at this gif instead, but that's no reason not to like my review! :D)<br><br>But, I really have to thank Logan. I really do. Because without his unfreakingbelieveable hotness, I wouldn't have watched the movie, and I would've never read the awesomeness of The Lightning Thief. <br><br>Yes, I loved the book. I've always taken an interest in Greek Mythology and I thought Rick Riordan's take on it was very unique, and unlike anything I've read before. <br><br>I absolutely loved Camp- Halfblood. Well, it sure seemed better than the budget summer camps I've been to. RR seriously out did himself with writing the camp. I could imagine everything vividly and I like to think that I know the camp from back to front. The cabins would have to be my favourite feature of the camp, though. If only they were like that in the camps I've been to. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380351823ra/705377.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Percy. What can I say? The guy has amazing underwater powers, is kick- ass and is a demigod. He's super loyal to his friends and family, is brave and has the looks (this is the part when you look at the gif of Logan Lerman again ;D). And he can make me laugh. Come on. You have to give a guy who make you laugh some credit. In short, the guy's the full package. <br><br>Another thing I loved were the other characters. Especially Annabeth, who looks like Cinderella in Percy's words (am I right? I don't have the book on me, sorry. Stupid library fines). And I'm expecting something to develop between her and Percy, if you know what I mean....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380351823ra/705378.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, yeah. I loved the book, it was exciting, fast- paced and humorous. Just one thing though, I'm kind of pissed that they didn't have cabins in the movie. Or Clarisse. Or the Oracle. Though it's hardly RR's fault. I just had to get it out there.<br> </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_28756899" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28756899" />
    <a title="Destinee Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90661-destinee-sutton"><img alt="Destinee Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1206569541p2/90661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28756899?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Destinee Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Destinee Sutton" href="/user/show/90661-destinee-sutton">Destinee Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Destinee by: </span>
      The children of SPL
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90661-destinee-sutton?shelf=harry-potter-alternative">harry-potter-alternative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90661-destinee-sutton?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90661-destinee-sutton?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer28756899&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28756899" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16166040918729543640">When I was about halfway through this book, I started making a list of its similarities to Harry Potter. Here is a sampling from that list:<br/><br/>1. There are three young heroes: a brainy girl (Annabeth/Hermione), a funny screw-up type (Grover/Ron), and a somewhat troubled but very brave lead (Harry/Percy).<br/><br/>2. People freak when the Harry/Percy character says the name of a powerful character. <br/><br/>3. The main bad guy (Kronos/Voldemort) is seeking to return to his former power, but most people are totally in d</span>
  <span id="freeText16166040918729543640" style="display:none">When I was about halfway through this book, I started making a list of its similarities to Harry Potter. Here is a sampling from that list:<br /><br />1. There are three young heroes: a brainy girl (Annabeth/Hermione), a funny screw-up type (Grover/Ron), and a somewhat troubled but very brave lead (Harry/Percy).<br /><br />2. People freak when the Harry/Percy character says the name of a powerful character. <br /><br />3. The main bad guy (Kronos/Voldemort) is seeking to return to his former power, but most people are totally in denial of that happening.<br /><br />4. The heroes train at a school that divides its students according to their character. (Chiron, the head trainer of the camp, equals Dumbledore.)<br /><br />5. Chiron/Dumbledore knows a prophecy about Percy/Harry but won't tell Percy/Harry what it is exactly.<br /><br />6. Percy/Harry has a gross stepfather named Smelly Gabe who protects him during his childhood, so Smelly Gabe obviously equals the Dursleys. <br /><br />7. Harry/Percy can talk to a certain animal because of his special gifts (Harry could talk to snakes, Percy can talk to horses). <br /><br />8. Riordan's three young heroes face down a three-headed dog at the end of their big quest, which if I'm not mistaken is exactly what happens in HP1 (granted, the three-headed dog is straight out of Greek mythology, so I should cut Riordan some slack on this one).<br /><br />I could go on (and on and on) which would be fun for me, but I won't. Instead, I'll shock you by saying that I totally loved this completely derivative book. It's super fun and fast-moving and the fact that it's kind of a HP rip-off actually makes me like it more. God, I loved Harry Potter. The Lighting Thief is like methadone. That might be what I said about the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/334123.The_Amulet_of_Samarkand__Bartimaeus_Trilogy___1_" title="The Amulet of Samarkand (Bartimaeus Trilogy, #1) by Jonathan Stroud" rel="nofollow noopener">The Amulet of Samarkand</a> but it's more true here. I can't wait to read the second one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16166040918729543640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_855244115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/855244115" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/855244115?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=quest">quest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=middle-school">middle-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=gary-stu">gary-stu</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=action">action</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer855244115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8530956171061721480"><blockquote>
  <i>Chiron looked surprised. “I thought that would be obvious enough. <b>The entrance to the Underworld is in Los Angeles.</b>”</i>
</blockquote>As someone who has worked in Los Angeles, I can tell you that this is completely accurate.<br/><br/>While Harry Potter was spending his summers at the Dursleys, Percy Jackson attended Camp Half-Blood. This book has done the impossible: <b>it has redeemed the name of Percy.</b><br/><br/>Yes, that's right, that snot-faced, lily-livered waste of air of the very same name from the <i>Harry Potter</i> universe. That</span>
  <span id="freeText8530956171061721480" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Chiron looked surprised. “I thought that would be obvious enough. <b>The entrance to the Underworld is in Los Angeles.</b>”</i>
</blockquote>As someone who has worked in Los Angeles, I can tell you that this is completely accurate.<br /><br />While Harry Potter was spending his summers at the Dursleys, Percy Jackson attended Camp Half-Blood. This book has done the impossible: <b>it has redeemed the name of Percy.</b><br /><br />Yes, that's right, that snot-faced, lily-livered waste of air of the very same name from the <i>Harry Potter</i> universe. That name is now relegated to the ranks of "acceptable," because of my love for this book.<br /><br />Perseus (Percy) Jackson is the kind of kid with whom you can't help sympathizing. He is the type that's born under a dark star, because inevitably, wherever he goes, whatever he does, however good his intentions, he can't help but fuck everything up. Everything that can, does and will go wrong. A simple field trip can turn into a disaster in seconds.<br /><br />Jay-Z's got 99 problems, Percy might have more. He nearly flunks all his classes, he's got dyslexia, he's got ADHD, and then there's Nancy Bobofit.<blockquote>
  <i>Nancy Bobofit appeared in front of me with her ugly friends—I guess she’d gotten tired of stealing from the tourists—and dumped her half-eaten lunch in Grover’s lap.<br />“Oops.” She grinned at me with her crooked teeth. Her freckles were orange, as if somebody had spray-painted her face with liquid Cheetos.</i>
</blockquote>Nancy Bobofit is not a major character in the book. I have to mention her because her character resounded with me. I had my own Nancy Bobofit back in grade school, only her name is Mimi. Nearly 2 decades later, the memory of her horrible face still makes me shudder. But I digress.<br /><br />As if the bullies aren't bad enough, his dad is a no-show, his stepfather is LITERALLY named Ugli, and there are crones foretelling Percy's death as well as a minotaur chasing his ass around. AND NOBODY'S TELLING HIM A SINGLE FUCKING THING. What's with all the secrecy, man?<br /><br />As it turned out, Percy is *whispers* special. He is a half-blood, meaning one of his parents is a Greek deity. He gets sent to Camp Half-Blood, with roughly 100 other kids like him.<br /><br />It's a freaky place for a kid who's known nothing but relative normalcy his entire life. All of a sudden, he's playing Pinochle with a Greek God (Dionysus---what a drunk), his best friend Grover turns out to be a satyr, and the gorgeous blond girl who rescues him thinks he's a doofus and she keeps calling him <b>"seaweed brain."</b><br /><br />To be fair, Percy had it coming. He is kind of a seaweed brain.<blockquote>
  <i>"Another time, Athena and Poseidon competed to be the patron god for the city of Athens. Your dad created some stupid saltwater spring for his gift. My mom created the olive tree. The people saw that her gift was better, so they named the city after her.”<br />“They must really like olives.”<br />“Oh, forget it.”<br />“Now, if she’d invented pizza—that I could understand.”<br />“I said, forget it!”</i>
</blockquote>Not your best moment, Percy.<br /><br />As it turned out, Percy IS special. His dad is one of the Big Three gods. Which kind of sucks, because that's not supposed to happen.<blockquote>
  <i>“About sixty years ago, after World War II, the Big Three agreed they wouldn’t sire any more heroes. Their children were just too powerful."</i>
</blockquote>A lot of people would think it was pretty cool to have such a powerful dad...not really.<blockquote>
  <i>Now that I was declared a son of one of the Big Three gods who weren’t supposed to have kids, I figured it was a crime for me just to be alive.</i>
</blockquote>Not only does Percy have to struggle to fit in at Camp Half-Blood, but there's some shit going on in Mount Olympus. The gods are fighting again (when are they not)...<blockquote>
  <i>"During the winter solstice, at the last council of the gods, Zeus and Poseidon had an argument. The usual nonsense: ‘Mother Rhea always liked you best,’ ‘Air disasters are more spectacular than sea disasters,’ et cetera."</i>
</blockquote>...and consequently, like a brother playing a prank on his younger siblings, someone's stuff was stolen. And Zeus thinks that his bro, Poseidon, put Percy up to it.<br /><br />Of course, blame the poor kid. Now Percy is shit out of luck YET AGAIN, and he's got no choice but to go on this huge stupid quest into the underworld (Los Angeles, ha!) to clear his name.<br /><br />He's not alone, he's accompanied by the <b>snarky, gorgeous, fiercely competent Annabeth</b> (she of the seaweed brain name-calling), as well as <b>the most incompetent satyr that ever lived</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>In his pocket was a set of reed pipes his daddy goat had carved for him, even though he only knew two songs: Mozart’s Piano Concerto no. 12 and Hilary Duff’s “So Yesterday,” both of which sounded pretty bad on reed pipes.</i>
</blockquote>It's going to be a loooooooong trip to the Underworld.<br /><br /><u>The Setting</u>: THIS. THIS IS HOW YOU DO GREEK MYTHOLOGY. I am a Greek mythology buff. I FUCKING LOVED THIS BOOK. This book is just absolutely fucking perfect in every way when it comes to rewriting and reinterpreting the Greek pantheon. It is so hilariously, awesomely irreverent, but completely fitting. The gods are reimagined, but they stay true to their true nature, and <b>the myths are retold in a cheeky, flippant manner that had me giggling my ass off</b>. This book is so fantastically snarky to the Greek gods. Everything is incredibly well-explained to a lay audience, like how the Greek gods can't seem to keep it in their pants.<blockquote>
  <i>Annabeth nodded. “Your father isn’t dead, Percy. He’s one of the Olympians.”<br />“That’s...crazy.”<br />“Is it? What’s the most common thing gods did in the old stories? They ran around falling in love with humans and having kids with them. Do you think they’ve changed their habits in the last few millennia?”</i>
</blockquote>And apparently, the habit runs true for both male and female goddesses.<blockquote>
  <i>“What? You assume it has to be a male god who finds a human female attractive? How sexist is that?”</i>
</blockquote><b>The existence of Greek gods and goddesses themselves are well explained, and believable.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Come now, Percy. What you call ‘Western civilization.’ Do you think it’s just an abstract concept? No, it’s a living force. A collective consciousness that has burned bright for thousands of years. The gods are part of it."<br />"Did the West die? The gods simply moved, to Germany, to France, to Spain, for a while. Wherever the flame was brightest, the gods were there. They spent several centuries in England. All you need to do is look at the architecture. People do not forget the gods."</i>
</blockquote>I had my doubts about the execution of the premise of Greek mythology, and all my doubts have been destroyed. <b>his book does great justice to the Greek gods, it is the most faithful rendition than I have ever read.</b><br /><br /><u>The Characters</u>: Yes, Percy is a special snowflake, but HELL, I LOVED THE LITTLE SHIT. He's got a special destiny. He is a special child. I DON'T CARE. Percy is such a sympathetic character, and although he won't be replacing Harry Potter in my heart any time soon, there is a special spot for him. He can give up pretty fast. He's kind of a wimp, but you know, finding out that you're a hald-blooded demigod is kind of a big deal, and I understand his attitude of "GET ME THE FUCK OUT OF HERE."<blockquote>
  <i>I didn’t know what else to do. I waved back.<br />“Don’t encourage them,” Annabeth warned. “Naiads are terrible flirts.”<br />“Naiads,” I repeated, feeling completely overwhelmed. “That’s it. I want to go home now.”</i>
</blockquote>He doesn't really want to do anything big. He's pretty stupid sometimes (Auntie Em, geez), he's not exactly heroic. He only does the heroic shit when there are no other options.<blockquote>
  <i>“All right,” I said. “It’s better than being turned into a dolphin.”</i>
</blockquote>I loved Annabeth, she is all I could want from a female supporting character. I can't say that I'm fond of Grover...but I can't help feeling that we'll be seeing more of him in the future.<blockquote>
  <i>“But a quest to . . .” Grover swallowed. “I mean, couldn’t the master bolt be in some place like Maine? Maine’s very nice this time of year.”</i>
</blockquote>Overall: a fantastic book. <b>A good middle grade book makes you feel like a child again, and this book did just the trick.</b> I found myself giggling throughout the book, and an hour after reading it, there's still a smile on my face that can't be wiped off.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8530956171061721480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/731077114?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer731077114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5869514457700173222">Were you a bit weird in school? Or are you still in school and think you're kinda weird? I mean, everyone is weird, but you know that I mean. Maybe you didn't fit in, maybe people thought you were a bit of a loser. Maybe you had learning difficulties, were a target for bullies, got into trouble a lot, maybe it seemed like your teachers just didn't like you. Maybe you sucked at reading and were even diagnosed with dyslexia. Or ADHD.<br/><br/>Well, don't worry. Truth is, you're actually most likely a child </span>
  <span id="freeText5869514457700173222" style="display:none">Were you a bit weird in school? Or are you still in school and think you're kinda weird? I mean, everyone is weird, but you know that I mean. Maybe you didn't fit in, maybe people thought you were a bit of a loser. Maybe you had learning difficulties, were a target for bullies, got into trouble a lot, maybe it seemed like your teachers just didn't like you. Maybe you sucked at reading and were even diagnosed with dyslexia. Or ADHD.<br /><br />Well, don't worry. Truth is, you're actually most likely a child of the gods with secret powers that enable you to zap those bullies and fulfill your true destiny. <b>Screw school, you've got bigger things to deal with anyway.</b> <br /><br />Lol, this book is amazing. My only regret is that I didn't have it when I was twelve years old because I would have read this until it was falling apart in my hands. Every insecure kid (so basically every kid) should read <i>The Lightning Thief</i>. I would want my hypothetical kids of the future to read this book. <b>It's the ultimate childhood fantasy</b> - discovering that everything people labelled as "weird" or negative about you is actually caused by your secret awesomeness. Pretty perfect message, if you ask me. <br /><br />I know, I know - this is plain old childhood wish fulfillment at its finest. But who cares? The best kids books are all about wish fulfillment to some extent and it's not like Percy Jackson doesn't have his fair share of enemies and heartache. It's the same idea that we all loved to buy into. The orphaned and neglected Harry Potter discovering he is a wizard. The nerdy loser-ish Peter Parker developing special abilities and becoming Spiderman. Children in the middle of WWII discovering a secret world through a wardrobe door in which they reign as royalty. Percy Jackson finding out he is the son of a god and has his own super powers. <br /><br />On top of the powerful message, this is a fast-paced exciting fantasy story full of friendships, Greek mythology, magic, mystery, bad guys and girls, and constant adventure. I enjoyed it now, despite me being a good ten years older than the target audience. I would have enjoyed it even more ten years ago. You should definitely go read this. Then, when you're done, give it to a kid to read too.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.leafmarks.com/emilymay" rel="nofollow noopener">Leafmarks</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5869514457700173222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2057436918?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 0786856297" href="/book/show/21473404-the-lightning-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2057436918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13973786918344128077">Believe it or not, but this was actually my first Rick Riordan book!!! <br/><br/><u>AND</u><br/><br/>I really enjoyed it!!! *lol*<br/><br/>This was such an epic adventure and I loved the countless hints and references to Greek Mythology! XD Rick Riordan’s approach definitely was a more than just funny one and I couldn’t help but had to laugh out loud whenever <b>Percy</b> opened his mouth! <br/>I swear that young boy is the embodiment of sass and the more I read about him, the more I got attached to this awesome boy! <3 I want to adopt Perseus</span>
  <span id="freeText13973786918344128077" style="display:none">Believe it or not, but this was actually my first Rick Riordan book!!! <br /><br /><u>AND</u><br /><br />I really enjoyed it!!! *lol*<br /><br />This was such an epic adventure and I loved the countless hints and references to Greek Mythology! XD Rick Riordan’s approach definitely was a more than just funny one and I couldn’t help but had to laugh out loud whenever <b>Percy</b> opened his mouth! <br />I swear that young boy is the embodiment of sass and the more I read about him, the more I got attached to this awesome boy! &lt;3 I want to adopt Perseus and if Poseidon doesn’t want him it’s his own fault! XD <br /><br />After reading the first book I don’t really feel a connection to <b>Annabeth</b>, but maybe this is going to change?! She seemed to be an interesting character and I liked their easy banter, altogether she was just too reserved for my taste though, which is pretty sad because I’m more than just certain that she’s actually a very cool girl! (On a side note: I really loved that she gave Percy the nickname “Seaweed Brain”! *lol* I’m fairly certain it could have been worse! ;-P)<br /><br />And <b>Grover</b>? Well, I guess I liked Grover as well! His habit to eat tin cans was a little unsettling but hey, I’m not going to judge him for his rather questionable diet. XD After all his heart is in the right place and when it comes down to it, this is everything that counts! ;-P I just hope he’ll survive his personal quest and I can’t help but wonder if we’re going to see him in one of the next books! <br /><br />Since my jump on the “Percy Jackson” train seems to be more than just a little delayed, I finally decided to leave it at that. I guess there is really nothing I could write or say that hasn’t been said already! I mean there are actually 55.567 reviews on goodreads! (Yes, I looked it up! ;-P) So yeah, I guess that says it all! XD<br /><br />If you haven’t had the pleasure to read the book yet I recommend you to do the following though:<br />Get a copy of <b>“The Lightning Thief”</b>, snuggle into your soft and comfy bed, ignore the bad autumn weather and enjoy the freaky ride! ;-P</span>
  <a data-text-id="13973786918344128077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_456983780" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/456983780" />
    <a title="Samadrita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13266158-samadrita"><img alt="Samadrita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461258628p2/13266158.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/456983780?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samadrita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samadrita" href="/user/show/13266158-samadrita">Samadrita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=loathed-this-book">loathed-this-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=should-not-have-been-published">should-not-have-been-published</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=abandoned-without-ado">abandoned-without-ado</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer456983780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5230391696206396648"><u>
  <b>EDIT 09/06/2013:-</b>
</u> That's it. I have had my fill of too many stupid, brain-cell destroying comments posted on this review in the past few months asking me to write a 'best-selling book' before attempting to take apart Rick Riordan's writing. As if the exclusive privilege of negatively criticizing a book is accorded only to published writers and not ordinary reviewers/readers. <br/>I <b>do</b> have the right to record my feelings about a book in <b>my</b> review. And it's such a shame that I am actually being fo</span>
  <span id="freeText5230391696206396648" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>EDIT 09/06/2013:-</b>
</u> That's it. I have had my fill of too many stupid, brain-cell destroying comments posted on this review in the past few months asking me to write a 'best-selling book' before attempting to take apart Rick Riordan's writing. As if the exclusive privilege of negatively criticizing a book is accorded only to published writers and not ordinary reviewers/readers. <br />I <b>do</b> have the right to record my feelings about a book in <b>my</b> review. And it's such a shame that I am actually being forced to put up this edit to make people aware of this fact. If this review hurts your sentiments as a fan, I am sorry I can't help you there. You must grow up and learn to let dichotomous opinions co-exist in harmony on the same page. That is all. <br /><br /><b>Caution:-</b> Brutal honesty ahead. Read at the expense of having to respect someone else's views.<br /><br />---------<br /><br />What a feeble attempt at recreating the Harry Potter magic! Aside from being highly unoriginal and unimaginative, the book grates on your nerves due to the frequency of Percy's lame attempts at sounding witty. Seriously, I'm supposed to laugh at his observations on the <i>'Bull Man'</i> and <i>'barnyard animals'</i>? <br />Not only did the writer not bother racking his brains to come up with a plot or a proper story, choosing instead to recycle key elements of the Harry Potter series, but he also ignored important aspects of a fantasy novel, one of which is the language. To call the narration just bad will be an understatement. Same can be said about the dialogue and the way the plot progresses - it's one cliched event unfolding after another. <br />The only novel thing about this book is the seamless integration of Greek mythology into a fantasy-based set-up. The 1 star is for that. <br />And so I'd like to put a premature end to my review because I just realized the futility of writing one of a book I hated. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5230391696206396648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5248748219254838098">I've read all (I think) of this series to my daughter, Celyn, but somehow this one escaped being reviewed until now.<br/><br/>I half-watched the film a year or two before we read this. Actually it was Rick reading (and being kind enough to review) my own trilogy that steered me toward picking up these books for Celyn (she's very disabled and can't read books for herself).<br/><br/>Anyway, it was a very good read. Celyn enjoyed the action and humour, and I enjoyed seeing the Greek legends I loved reading about as a </span>
  <span id="freeText5248748219254838098" style="display:none">I've read all (I think) of this series to my daughter, Celyn, but somehow this one escaped being reviewed until now.<br /><br />I half-watched the film a year or two before we read this. Actually it was Rick reading (and being kind enough to review) my own trilogy that steered me toward picking up these books for Celyn (she's very disabled and can't read books for herself).<br /><br />Anyway, it was a very good read. Celyn enjoyed the action and humour, and I enjoyed seeing the Greek legends I loved reading about as a kid given a new lease of life, offered up to the most recent generation.<br /><br />It starts off with that irresistible device beloved of fantasy books that you (vicariously the hero) were meant for more than this regular old world and that all those odd things you don't understand about everyday life ... really are odd and full of special meaning. In fact ... your dad's a god, and not just any old god but Poseidon himself. And that means you're part god yourself! Hoorah!<br /><br />So Percy gets inducted into hero school, makes friends with good monsters, fights and kills bad ones, and dives into adventure.<br /><br />The hero school (Camp Halfblood) has demi-gods descended from all the Greek mythos, which makes for fun conflicts. Meanwhile in the wider world there are rumblings that the titans (from whom the gods wrested control of the world at the dawn of time) are about to stage a comeback. Zeus has lost his lightning bolt and the thief must be found before the gods fall to blows and Olympus topples.<br /><br />The genius is in the mix of modern day America with all its kitsch, landmarks, cities etc with mythical Greece. It shouldn't really work, but does. And to cap it all, your kid is getting a classical education on the sly!<br /><br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br /><br />…...<br /></span>

Lol <br><br>Happy Reading! <br><br>Mel ♥<br><br>•••••••••••<br><b>First Reading</b><br><br>I am <b>FINALLY</b> getting around to reading this series. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479747103i/21231096._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I thought the movies were okay, I do wish they would remake them and make them better, like the books =) <br><br>Poor Percy. <br><br><b>Look, I didn't want to be a half-blood. <br>If you're reading this because you think you might be one, my advice is: close the book right now. Most of the time, it gets you killed in painful, nasty ways. <br><br>If you're a normal kid, reading this because you think it's fiction, great. Read on. They get attacked by many creatures of all shapes and sizes. They also get help from certain creatures and a pink poodle named Gladiola who ran away from home and doesn't want to go back but does so the kids can have some reward money. Wasn't that sweet! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479747103i/21231098.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>↑ Can you blame little Gladiola? I mean I love the color pink, but NO, JUST NO! <br><br>Anyhoo, I did want to smack the group a few times because of stupid things, but who doesn't do those from time to time. *raises hand* I loved when they saved the animals in the old truck they were riding in, Grover is awesome! <br><br>I look forward to reading ALL of the other 50 billion books in this ongoing Rick Riordan world! ♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/11/percy-jackson-and-olympians-lightning.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1623883546?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer45532257275566713">this is one of the most common books that pops up on my feed. no joke. i probably see this at least a couple times a week, so i finally gave in and read it! yay me! hehe.<br/><br/>i will admit, this is the first time i have read a middle grade novel since i was that age, but i have to hand it to rick riordan. this story is sooo unique, which is hard to do considering how many fantasy novels are out there for young readers. and i have no doubt that, if i had first read when i was a kid, i would have been b</span>
  <span id="freeText45532257275566713" style="display:none">this is one of the most common books that pops up on my feed. no joke. i probably see this at least a couple times a week, so i finally gave in and read it! yay me! hehe.<br /><br />i will admit, this is the first time i have read a middle grade novel since i was that age, but i have to hand it to rick riordan. this story is sooo unique, which is hard to do considering how many fantasy novels are out there for young readers. and i have no doubt that, if i had first read when i was a kid, i would have been beyond OBSESSED with it. it makes me so sad to think that my childhood missed out on this series. <br /><br />but reading this as an adult is an entirely different experience. i can appreciate this for what it is, which is fun and exciting, but it honestly just made me feel old as it has a very juvenile feel to it. i have heard some of riordans other books are aimed towards older readers, so i may give them a shot since i do love me some greek mythology!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_383475847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/383475847" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/383475847?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/22456224-the-lightning-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer383475847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11732255183787834841">My inner child is absolutely devastated that I didn't read this series when I was a kid. Percy Jackson was one of those series that was always there, just on the periphery of my social conscious. I knew I should read it, but for one reason or another I gravitated to other things instead. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490397182ra/22310002.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Thankfully, as an adult who likes reviewing books for fun in my spare time, I have absolutely no shame about reading the series now, even if it was originally intended for a younger audience. In some ways, I thi</span>
  <span id="freeText11732255183787834841" style="display:none">My inner child is absolutely devastated that I didn't read this series when I was a kid. Percy Jackson was one of those series that was always there, just on the periphery of my social conscious. I knew I should read it, but for one reason or another I gravitated to other things instead. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490397182ra/22310002.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Thankfully, as an adult who likes reviewing books for fun in my spare time, I have absolutely no shame about reading the series now, even if it was originally intended for a younger audience. In some ways, I think I might have even enjoyed it more as an adult. <br><br>I'm a huge fan of Greek mythology. (I may or may not have filled electives in high school and college with classes on mythology; just like I may or may not have obsessed over shows like Xena and Hercules in my teenage years.) I had a great time comparing my own personal knowledge of Greek mythology against the ways that Riordan weaves the stories into Percy's larger adventure.<br><br>It's such a fun way to introduce Greek mythology to children and teens while staying entertaining for adults as well! The mythology remains faithful to the original stories, but it feels fresh and fun here as each character is full of personality and charm. The world is full of magic and wonder and I never once felt bored as the characters explored within it. <br><br>Speaking of characters full of personality, Percy Jackson himself is one of my new faves in terms of characterization. He's brave, loyal and hilarious and his friendship with Grover and Annabeth has quickly become a favorite for me. Also, can I just say that I think it's so cute that Riordan based Percy on his son, who had been diagnosed with ADHD and dyslexia? I think it's so awesome that Percy gets to sort of stand apart from other heroes in stories as a champion for those kids forevermore. <br><br>When I finished reading this book, I immediately went and told my 11 year old nephew that he absolutely had to read this book so I had someone to talk to about it. I'm proud to call myself a Percy Jackson fan and will be continuing the rest of the series shortly! <br><br>★★★★★ = 5 stars! <br><br>See this review and more on my blog: <a href="https://bookbastion.wordpress.com/2017/03/25/the-lightning-thief/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Bastion</a> my blog: <br>__________________<br><br>Can ya'll believe I've never read this series before? I picked up the first 3 books on a whim the other day and am excited to give it a go. <br><br>RTC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11732255183787834841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81215929" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81215929" />
    <a title="Cara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1876075-cara"><img alt="Cara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350665534p2/1876075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81215929?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara" href="/user/show/1876075-cara">Cara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780786856299" href="/book/show/893174.The_Lightning_Thief">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">reluctant readers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cara by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1947904-gerson">Gerson</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=books-made-into-movies">books-made-into-movies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81215929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6146753399269069112">Really is there something I could say that hasn't been said? Doubtful, but in utterly stupid human style I will write a review anyway attempting to tell people how cool this book is.<br/><br/>This is plainly an <b> awesome </b> idea. I had always wondered what happened to the kids of half gods/goddess and humans. Here's the story to quench your curiosity. Percy Jackson has been dumped around from border school to border school. He has never been quite like anybody else, but as the end of sixth grade approaches h</span>
  <span id="freeText6146753399269069112" style="display:none">Really is there something I could say that hasn't been said? Doubtful, but in utterly stupid human style I will write a review anyway attempting to tell people how cool this book is.<br /><br />This is plainly an <b> awesome </b> idea. I had always wondered what happened to the kids of half gods/goddess and humans. Here's the story to quench your curiosity. Percy Jackson has been dumped around from border school to border school. He has never been quite like anybody else, but as the end of sixth grade approaches he'll find out how unique he actually is...<br /><br />I picked this up thinking that I would enjoy it, but not to the extent of really being <u> hooked </u> so fast. Literally from the first pages I knew I was gonna finish this book. It's geared towards middle grade readers and mostly male I think, but really all that goes away when you're reading this. As an older reader I did see most of the twists coming but that is because the author is generous about hints, which I have always liked. What really sold it for me though is the action. I have mentioned this numerous times, but I'll say it again, <i> I am a total sucker for action scenes </i>. Give me a good fight sequence and I'm there. <br /><br />A few reviews mention how this is ripoff of Harry Potter, and now that I think about it I could see where they are coming from. There are definitely similarities, but to be honest I didn't really catch that, (I guess I'm kind of dim...I shouldn't probably admit to that *shakes head* moving on) because the world the author set was so original that the similar setup can be easily forgiven.<br /><br />We all love heroes. Especially ones like Percy. People never expect much from him, and that's what makes this journey of his so personal to the reader. You root for him and are so glad that his muscling his way through it. It has the feel of cheering for the underdog. And I'm guessing this underdog is going to blow everyone out of the water.<br /><br /><b>Extra Note:</b> Oh glorious goodness they made a movie! <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xko1Mx5w4tg" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a> is a link to the movie trailer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6146753399269069112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4098163204569520566">A list of reasons I love this book, brought to you by Nostalgia™:<br/><br/>- clickbait chapter titles<br/>- middle grade book that doesn’t write down to its audience<br/>- percy jackson was my first book boyfriend and remains the most iconic of my middle school crushes<br/>- <s>I kind of like him better than harry potter???</s><br/>- he mails the severed head of a monster to the fucking gods bc they weren't being appreciative enough of him<br/>- basically, the son of the sea god is literally and figuratively salty<br/>- annabeth is only 12 y</span>
  <span id="freeText4098163204569520566" style="display:none">A list of reasons I love this book, brought to you by Nostalgia™:<br /><br />- clickbait chapter titles<br />- middle grade book that doesn’t write down to its audience<br />- percy jackson was my first book boyfriend and remains the most iconic of my middle school crushes<br />- <s>I kind of like him better than harry potter???</s><br />- he mails the severed head of a monster to the fucking gods bc they weren't being appreciative enough of him<br />- basically, the son of the sea god is literally and figuratively salty<br />- annabeth is only 12 yet so fucking smart and badass??? I want to adopt her<br />- grover is a sweet, smol vegetarian who will forever have a special place in my heart<br />- also he talks about food in his sleep<br />- features a main character with ADHD and dyslexia<br />- mythology is incorporated into the modern world in absolutely flawless and endlessly clever ways<br />- it’s just so much fun?????<br /><br />This was the first book series I think I truly <i>loved</i> as a child after Harry Potter, and I honestly don’t know why I waited so long to reread this. It’s fun and smart and also kind of emotional <s>but maybe that’s just me bc I have an unhealthy attachment to these characters</s>.<br /><br />If you’ve already read this, you should reread it, and if you haven’t, <b>please do!!!!!!</b> My br partner hadn’t read this before and she loved it anyway, so I stand by my belief that the nostalgia factor isn’t necessary to enjoy this book as an adult! 💙<br /><br />---------------------------<br /><br />rereading this with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42130592" rel="nofollow noopener">matthew gray gubler's #1 fangirl</a> bc we need something fun to get us out of our slump :)))</span>

<div id="review_131037970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131037970" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131037970?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=and-so-this-is-grad-school">and-so-this-is-grad-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131037970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8409605807333914721">this is a perfect book for young teenagers. if you were trying to devise a formula for writing a perfect book for this age group, you could not have done much better than this.<br/><br/>1) mysterious parentage. kids are totally self-absorbed. some never grow out of it, of course, but in younger people, it is more excusable - their internal life makes up the majority of their experience, they are used to being the center of attention and they spend <b>a lot</b> of time thinking about themselves and fantasizing. s</span>
  <span id="freeText8409605807333914721" style="display:none">this is a perfect book for young teenagers. if you were trying to devise a formula for writing a perfect book for this age group, you could not have done much better than this.<br><br>1) mysterious parentage. kids are totally self-absorbed. some never grow out of it, of course, but in younger people, it is more excusable - their internal life makes up the majority of their experience, they are used to being the center of attention and they spend <b>a lot</b> of time thinking about themselves and fantasizing. so having romantic, mysterious origins is the best thing ever - "maybe i am the son/daughter of a god/goddess/russian count, etc..." i still wonder about that, even though it is clear where i came from.<br><br>2) this book has excellent gender equality, so it appeals to both younger girls and boys. goddesses are just as cool as gods, and their children are equally badass. this is rarely the case in teen adventure lit. (see <i>naruto</i>)<br><br>3) this makes history class relevant.(or wherever it is that kids learn about those wacky greeks) personifying the gods and goddesses makes them more recognizable and immediate for kids; bringing old litterature aliiiive and all that. and they will definitely learn not to mix up chiron and charon.<br><br>4) but it is also wonderfully subversive. it is all about polytheism and it makes the point that what we consider mythology today used to be a very real belief system for tons of people. any bright kid is going to make the logical leap to thinking about contemporary religion and how one day, it may well fall under mythology for students of the future, and how any current religious disagreements will be just like poseidon and athena's quarrels. because of this, i am surprised that this series has not been more frequently challenged/banned. oh, i know why, because the people most likely to challenge shit are not themselves capable of making that logical leap; they operate solely on knee-jerk see-a-bad-word reactions.<br><br>but this book is great - it has fantastic pacing, the characters are incredibly appealing, i like the premise, and i really really like that it is five books only. i will definitely read the rest of these puppies when i get around to it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8409605807333914721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14850927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer374981152122742643">6/9/20:<br/><br/>Some friends and I are doing a reread of this series in light of the TV series announcement, so yeah! Finished rereading this one for the...fourth time I guess? And I truly never tire of it, still one of my absolute favorite books/series of all time. <br/><br/>I feel like my previous reviews pretty much sum up my thoughts so I’ll just leave it at that haha, anyway my older reviews of it are below. <br/><br/>—<br/><br/><b>Yet another review (5/30/14):</b><br/><br/>Well I feel like I've rewritten/updated my review of this like a billion</span>
  <span id="freeText374981152122742643" style="display:none">6/9/20:<br /><br />Some friends and I are doing a reread of this series in light of the TV series announcement, so yeah! Finished rereading this one for the...fourth time I guess? And I truly never tire of it, still one of my absolute favorite books/series of all time. <br /><br />I feel like my previous reviews pretty much sum up my thoughts so I’ll just leave it at that haha, anyway my older reviews of it are below. <br /><br />—<br /><br /><b>Yet another review (5/30/14):</b><br /><br />Well I feel like I've rewritten/updated my review of this like a billion times at this point, but I'm here to do it again. I re-read this over the span of the past two days when I had to take two super-long bus trips. This was the third time I've read the whole thing, I'm pretty sure (kind of the fourth time I guess, since I read a lot of it out loud to my younger siblings last year). There are few books that I loved when I was 12 that I still deeply love now, and this is one of those few books. In fact, the more times I read it the more I fall in love with it. I adore the series as a whole and think it develops so wonderfully as it goes along, and sometimes I almost forget how great the first book is. Maybe it's not the strongest of the series, but it's still fantastic. It's exciting, it's hilarious, there are so many lovable characters and great character development/backstories/etc. and as a giant mythology nerd I love how all the Greek myths are tied in and modernized. The rest of the series just gets better and better, and I love the Heroes of Olympus series as well––and it always makes me happy to go back to where it all started, and remember why I first fell in love with this book/series nine years ago. (Gosh that makes me feel old.)<br /><br />------<br /><br />Old/crappier review from like two years ago under the spoiler.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hmm my old review for this kind of sucked. I feel like I've rewritten this review like twenty times, but oh well. <br /><br />I guess I just can't do this book justice. Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians is one of my favorite series, despite the fact that I think it's probably aimed more toward 12-year-old boys, and ... well, I'm a 19-year-old girl. But I can't help it. I fell in love with these books when I was around 12 and I never outgrew them (which is something I can't say for most books I liked when I was 12).<br /><br />You know what's freaky? So, my friend and I went to a Rick Riordan book signing recently. (And that's not the freaky part, although seeing him in person was pretty freaky.) Anyway, we're standing there and I'm like, "OMG ... A lot of these kids were, like, not even born yet the first time we read The Lightning Thief." We were kind of surrounded by little 7-year-old boys it seemed like. But anyway, IT WAS STILL AWESOME. And really there was no point to this story except to prove my point ... that I have loved these books for a long, long time.<br /><br />Everything about these books is just totally lovable. The characters are great, the character relationships are nicely developed, the story is exciting, all the Greek mythology is tied in brilliantly, the humor is laugh-out-loud hilarious. Mannn, I could go on and on. And they just get better with each book. I frequently pick these up and read parts of them just to make me feel better. They're an instant pick-me-up. <br /><br />Also, random side note: the movie was just ... horrible. I could go on a long rant about it, but I won't because that would be annoying. Let's just focus on how awesome the book is.<br /><br />These books are just beastly awesome, and if you have not read them I pity your depraved soul. Go read them now. If you have read the book and seen the movie, I am crying with you right now. If you have seen the movie and not read the book … well, something is wrong with you. Go read the book, for crying out loud! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14124549265808130131"><b>4.5 Golden stars</b><br/><br/>before I start talking about how awesome this book/series is; I should say:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589221934ra/29456970.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>&<br/>second,<br/><br/><i>"Read Rick Riordan's books in English or you miss half the FUN!"</i><br/><br/>I saw that happened!<br/><br/>This Book/Series/Universe is a "must read" to anyone who loves myths, Regardless of Age. (I read it first when I was 22 & fell in love with it immediately by the first sentence (which was the chapter's title!)) though it probably depends on you have active inner child & love mythology in modern days with lots of fun</span>
  <span id="freeText14124549265808130131" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Golden stars</b><br><br>before I start talking about how awesome this book/series is; I should say:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589221934ra/29456970.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>&amp;<br>second,<br><br><i>"Read Rick Riordan's books in English or you miss half the FUN!"</i><br><br>I saw that happened!<br><br>This Book/Series/Universe is a "must read" to anyone who loves myths, Regardless of Age. (I read it first when I was 22 &amp; fell in love with it immediately by the first sentence (which was the chapter's title!)) though it probably depends on you have active inner child &amp; love mythology in modern days with lots of fun or not too. (my dad liked it.)<br>it's an art to write a book suitable for everyone. &lt;3<br>&amp; Percy's character reminded me of one of my teenage years bookish crushes, Bobby in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/42782-pendragon" rel="nofollow noopener">Pendragon</a> series by D. J. MacHale; sassy, quick witty comebacks with funny thoughts &amp; comparisons in the narration.<br><br>First book in the masterpiece of Riordanverse,<br>First book in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/183923-camp-half-blood-chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">Camp Half-Blood Chronicles</a><br>I LOVE ALL UNCLE RICK'S BOOKS!<br><br>the way it started, from the very first page, it shows &amp; promises how amazing &amp; funny it would be. I mean, just look at the chapters name!<br>I laughed with almost every sentences!<br>(also full of "I-can-relate" moments!)<br><br>2019: I read this for my dad &amp; he actually liked it very much. another proof for this story is regardless of age XD (also I was a very good narrator.)<br>finished a day before Percy's 26th birthday! [August 17]<br>I'm a sucker fror finding relatable things in my life &amp; my fandoms. :D<br>-<br>plot (excitements): ★★★★/5<br>the start was amazing <br>also the way magic &amp; myths related the real world &amp; wrapping up the story.<br>I love this way that myths got modernized.<br>in general, full of excitements &amp; surprises!<br>-<br>World building: ★★★★★/5<br>the real world &amp; its relation to myths world, is very realistic, the way I can assume it is real &amp; actually can be happening somewhere!<br>-<br>Characters: ★★★★★/5<br>many lovable characters!<br>Percy is awesome. <br>also Grover &amp; Annabeth&lt;3<br>&amp; Sally Jackson is an Angel! strong &amp; supportive.<br>-<br>Written style: ★★★★★/5<br>even though it is first person view, but Percy is awesome narrative. &amp; Riordan KNOWS how to write FUNNY &amp; also giving us the Adrenaline Surge!<br><br>HUMOR!: ★★★★★/5<br>LOL like after every sentence!<br><br><i> “She'd also called me brave...unless she was talking to the catfish.” </i><br>-<br>Cover: ★★★★★/5<br>-<br>General idea: ★★★★★/5<br>Real world+Mythology+Fantasy: Sign me in</span>
